"2294"	"superiority attached to any person who hailed from Old Virginia; and"
"2295"	"this superiority was exalted to supremacy when a person of such nativity"
"2296"	"could also prove descent from the First Families of that great"
"2297"	"commonwealth. The Howards and Driscolls were of this aristocracy. In"
"2298"	"their eyes it was a nobility. It had its unwritten laws, and they were"
"2299"	"as clearly defined and as strict as any that could be found among the"
"2300"	"printed statutes of the land. The F. F. V. was born a gentleman; his"
"2301"	"highest duty in life was to watch over that great inheritance and keep"
"2302"	"it unsmirched. He must keep his honor spotless. Those laws were his"
"2303"	"chart; his course was marked out on it; if he swerved from it by so much"
"2304"	"as half a point of the compass it meant shipwreck to his honor; that is"
"2305"	"to say, degradation from his rank as a gentleman. These laws required"
"2306"	"certain things of him which his religion might forbid: then his religion"
"2307"	"must yield--the laws could not be relaxed to accommodate religions or"
"2308"	"anything else. Honor stood first; and the laws defined what it was and"
"2309"	"wherein it differed in certain details from honor as defined by church"
"2310"	"creeds and by the social laws and customs of some of the minor divisions"
"2311"	"of the globe that had got crowded out when the sacred boundaries of"
"2312"	"Virginia were staked out."
"2313"	"If Judge Driscoll was the recognized first citizen of Dawson's Landing,"
"2314"	"Pembroke Howard was easily its recognized second citizen. He was called"
"2315"	"\"the great lawyer\"--an earned title. He and Driscoll were of the same"
"2316"	"age--a year or two past sixty."
"2317"	"Although Driscoll was a free-thinker and Howard a strong and determined"
"2318"	"Presbyterian, their warm intimacy suffered no impairment in consequence."
"2319"	"They were men whose opinions were their own property and not subject to"
"2320"	"revision and amendment, suggestion or criticism, by anybody, even their"
"2321"	"friends."
"2322"	"The day's fishing finished, they came floating down stream in their"
"2323"	"skiff, talking national politics and other high matters, and presently"
"2324"	"met a skiff coming up from town, with a man in it who said:"
"2325"	"\"I reckon you know one of the new twins gave your nephew a kicking last"
"2326"	"night, Judge?\""
"2327"	"\"Did what?\""
"2328"	"\"Gave him a kicking.\""
"2329"	"The old Judge's lips paled, and his eyes began to flame. He choked with"
"2330"	"anger for a moment, then he got out what he was trying to say--"
"2331"	"\"Well--well--go on! give me the details!\""
"2332"	"The man did it. At the finish the Judge was silent a minute, turning"
"2333"	"over in his mind the shameful picture of Tom's flight over the"
"2334"	"footlights; then he said, as if musing aloud--\"H'm--I don't understand"
"2335"	"it. I was asleep at home. He didn't wake me. Thought he was competent to"
"2336"	"manage his affair without my help, I reckon.\" His face lit up with pride"
"2337"	"and pleasure at that thought, and he said with a cheery complacency, \"I"
"2338"	"like that--it's the true old blood--hey, Pembroke?\""
"2339"	"Howard smiled an iron smile, and nodded his head approvingly. Then the"
"2340"	"news-bringer spoke again--"
"2341"	"\"But Tom beat the twin on the trial.\""
"2342"	"The Judge looked at the man wonderingly, and said--"
"2343"	"\"The trial? What trial?\""
"2344"	"\"Why, Tom had him up before Judge Robinson for assault and battery.\""
"2345"	"The old man shrank suddenly together like one who has received a"
"2346"	"death-stroke. Howard sprang for him as he sank forward in a swoon, and"
"2347"	"took him in his arms, and bedded him on his back in the boat. He"
"2348"	"sprinkled water in his face, and said to the startled visitor--"
"2349"	"\"Go, now--don't let him come to and find you here. You see what an"
"2350"	"effect your heedless speech has had; you ought to have been more"
"2351"	"considerate than to blurt out such a cruel piece of slander as that.\""
"2352"	"\"I'm right down sorry I did it now, Mr. Howard, and I wouldn't have done"
"2353"	"it if I had thought: but it ain't slander; it's perfectly true, just as"
"2354"	"I told him.\""
"2355"	"He rowed away. Presently the old Judge came out of his faint and looked"
"2356"	"up piteously into the sympathetic face that was bent over him."
"2357"	"\"Say it ain't true, Pembroke; tell me it ain't true!\" he said in a weak"
"2358"	"voice."
"2359"	"There was nothing weak in the deep organ-tones that responded--"
"2360"	"\"You know it's a lie as well as I do, old friend. He is of the best"
"2361"	"blood of the Old Dominion.\""
"2362"	"\"God bless you for saying it!\" said the old gentleman, fervently. \"Ah,"
"2363"	"Pembroke, it was such a blow!\""
"2364"	"Howard stayed by his friend, and saw him home, and entered the house"
"2365"	"with him. It was dark, and past supper-time, but the Judge was not"
"2366"	"thinking of supper; he was eager to hear the slander refuted from"
"2367"	"headquarters, and as eager to have Howard hear it, too. Tom was sent"
"2368"	"for, and he came immediately. He was bruised and lame, and was not a"
"2369"	"happy-looking object. His uncle made him sit down, and said--"
"2370"	"\"We have been hearing about your adventure, Tom, with a handsome lie"
"2371"	"added to it for embellishment. Now pulverize that lie to dust! What"
"2372"	"measures have you taken? How does the thing stand?\""
"2373"	"Tom answered guilelessly: \"It don't stand at all; it's all over. I had"
"2374"	"him up in court and beat him. Pudd'nhead Wilson defended him--first case"
"2375"	"he ever had, and lost it. The judge fined the miserable hound five"
"2376"	"dollars for the assault.\""
"2377"	"Howard and the Judge sprang to their feet with the opening"
"2378"	"sentence--why, neither knew; then they stood gazing vacantly at each"
"2379"	"other. Howard stood a moment, then sat mournfully down without saying"
"2380"	"anything. The Judge's wrath began to kindle, and he burst out--"
"2381"	"\"You cur! You scum! You vermin! Do you mean to tell me that blood of my"
"2382"	"race has suffered a blow and crawled to a court of law about it? Answer"
"2383"	"me!\""
"2384"	"Tom's head drooped, and he answered with an eloquent silence. His uncle"
"2385"	"stared at him with a mixed expression of amazement and shame and"
"2386"	"incredulity that was sorrowful to see. At last he said--"
"2387"	"\"Which of the twins was it?\""
"2388"	"\"Count Luigi.\""
"2389"	"\"You have challenged him?\""
"2390"	"\"N--no,\" hesitated Tom, turning pale."
"2391"	"\"You will challenge him to-night. Howard will carry it.\""
"2392"	"Tom began to turn sick, and to show it. He turned his hat round and"
"2393"	"round in his hand, his uncle glowering blacker and blacker upon him as"
"2394"	"the heavy seconds drifted by; then at last he began to stammer, and said"
"2395"	"piteously--"
"2396"	"\"Oh, please don't ask me to do it, uncle! He is a murderous devil--I"
"2397"	"never could--I--I'm afraid of him!\""
"2398"	"Old Driscoll's mouth opened and closed three times before he could get"
"2399"	"it to perform its office; then he stormed out--"
"2400"	"\"A coward in my family! A Driscoll a coward! Oh, what have I done to"
"2401"	"deserve this infamy!\" He tottered to his secretary in the corner"
"2402"	"repeating that lament again and again in heartbreaking tones, and got"
"2403"	"out of a drawer a paper, which he slowly tore to bits scattering the"
"2404"	"bits absently in his track as he walked up and down the room, still"
"2405"	"grieving and lamenting. At last he said--"
"2406"	"\"There it is, shreds and fragments once more--my will. Once more you"
"2407"	"have forced me to disinherit you, you base son of a most noble father!"
"2408"	"Leave my sight! Go--before I spit on you!\""
"2409"	"The young man did not tarry. Then the Judge turned to Howard:"
"2410"	"\"You will be my second, old friend?\""
"2411"	"\"Of course.\""
"2412"	"\"There is pen and paper. Draft the cartel, and lose no time.\""
"2413"	"\"The Count shall have it in his hands in fifteen minutes,\" said Howard."
"2414"	"Tom was very heavy-hearted. His appetite was gone with his property and"
"2415"	"his self-respect. He went out the back way and wandered down the obscure"
"2416"	"lane grieving, and wondering if any course of future conduct, however"
"2417"	"discreet and carefully perfected and watched over, could win back his"
"2418"	"uncle's favor and persuade him to reconstruct once more that generous"
"2419"	"will which had just gone to ruin before his eyes. He finally concluded"
"2420"	"that it could. He said to himself that he had accomplished this sort of"
"2421"	"triumph once already, and that what had been done once could be done"
"2422"	"again. He would set about it. He would bend every energy to the task,"
"2423"	"and he would score that triumph once more, cost what it might to his"
"2424"	"convenience, limit as it might his frivolous and liberty-loving life."
"2425"	"\"To begin,\" he said to himself, \"I'll square up with the proceeds of my"
"2426"	"raid, and then gambling has got to be stopped--and stopped short off."
"2427"	"It's the worst vice I've got--from my standpoint, anyway, because it's"
"2428"	"the one he can most easily find out, through the impatience of my"
"2429"	"creditors. He thought it expensive to have to pay two hundred dollars to"
"2430"	"them for me once. Expensive--that! Why, it cost me the whole of his"
"2431"	"fortune--but of course he never thought of that; some people can't think"
"2432"	"of any but their own side of a case. If he had known how deep I am in,"
"2433"	"now, the will would have gone to pot without waiting for a duel to help."
"2434"	"Three hundred dollars! It's a pile! But he'll never hear of it, I'm"
"2435"	"thankful to say. The minute I've cleared it off, I'm safe; and I'll"
"2436"	"never touch a card again. Anyway, I won't while he lives, I make oath to"
"2437"	"that. I'm entering on my last reform--I know it--yes, and I'll win; but"
"2438"	"after that, if I ever slip again I'm gone.\""
"2439"	"CHAPTER XIII."
"2440"	"Tom Stares at Ruin."
"2441"	"When I reflect upon the number of disagreeable people who I know have"
"2442"	"gone to a better world, I am moved to lead a different life.--Pudd'nhead"
"2443"	"Wilson's Calendar."
"2444"	"October. This is one of the peculiarly dangerous months to speculate in"
"2445"	"stocks in. The others are July, January, September, April, November,"
"2446"	"May, March, June, December, August, and February.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's"
"2447"	"Calendar."
"2448"	"Thus mournfully communing with himself Tom moped along the lane past"
"2449"	"Pudd'nhead Wilson's house, and still on and on between fences inclosing"
"2450"	"vacant country on each hand till he neared the haunted house, then he"
"2451"	"came moping back again, with many sighs and heavy with trouble. He"
"2452"	"sorely wanted cheerful company. Rowena! His heart gave a bound at the"
"2453"	"thought, but the next thought quieted it--the detested twins would be"
"2454"	"there."
"2455"	"He was on the inhabited side of Wilson's house, and now as he approached"
"2456"	"it he noticed that the sitting-room was lighted. This would do; others"
"2457"	"made him feel unwelcome sometimes, but Wilson never failed in courtesy"
"2458"	"toward him, and a kindly courtesy does at least save one's feelings,"
"2459"	"even if it is not professing to stand for a welcome. Wilson heard"
"2460"	"footsteps at his threshold, then the clearing of a throat."
"2461"	"\"It's that fickle-tempered, dissipated young goose--poor devil, he find"
"2462"	"friends pretty scarce to-day, likely, after the disgrace of carrying a"
"2463"	"personal-assault case into a law-court.\""
"2464"	"A dejected knock. \"Come in!\""
"2465"	"Tom entered, and drooped into a chair, without saying anything. Wilson"
"2466"	"said kindly--"
"2467"	"\"Why, my boy, you look desolate. Don't take it so hard. Try and forget"
"2468"	"you have been kicked.\""
"2469"	"\"Oh, dear,\" said Tom, wretchedly, \"it's not that, Pudd'nhead--it's not"
"2470"	"that. It's a thousand times worse than that--oh, yes, a million times"
"2471"	"worse.\""
"2472"	"\"Why, Tom, what do you mean? Has Rowena--\""
"2473"	"\"Flung me? No, but the old man has.\""
"2474"	"Wilson said to himself, \"Aha!\" and thought of the mysterious girl in the"
"2475"	"bedroom. \"The Driscolls have been making discoveries!\" Then he said"
"2476"	"aloud, gravely:"
"2477"	"\"Tom, there are some kinds of dissipation which--\""
"2478"	"\"Oh, shucks, this hasn't got anything to do with dissipation. He wanted"
"2479"	"me to challenge that derned Italian savage, and I wouldn't do it.\""
"2480"	"\"Yes, of course he would do that,\" said Wilson in a meditative"
"2481"	"matter-of-course way, \"but the thing that puzzled me was, why he didn't"
"2482"	"look to that last night, for one thing, and why he let you carry such a"
"2483"	"matter into a court of law at all, either before the duel or after it."
"2484"	"It's no place for it. It was not like him. I couldn't understand it. How"
"2485"	"did it happen?\""
"2486"	"\"It happened because he didn't know anything about it. He was asleep"
"2487"	"when I got home last night.\""
"2488"	"\"And you didn't wake him? Tom, is that possible?\""
"2489"	"Tom was not getting much comfort here. He fidgeted a moment, then said:"
"2490"	"\"I didn't choose to tell him--that's all. He was going a-fishing before"
"2491"	"dawn, with Pembroke Howard, and if I got the twins into the common"
"2492"	"calaboose--and I thought sure I could--I never dreamed of their slipping"
"2493"	"out on a paltry fine for such an outrageous offense--well, once in the"
"2494"	"calaboose they would be disgraced, and uncle wouldn't want any duels"
"2495"	"with that sort of characters, and wouldn't allow any.\""
"2496"	"\"Tom, I am ashamed of you! I don't see how you could treat your good old"
"2497"	"uncle so. I am a better friend of his than you are; for if I had known"
"2498"	"the circumstances I would have kept that case out of court until I got"
"2499"	"word to him and let him have a gentleman's chance.\""
"2500"	"\"You would?\" exclaimed Tom, with lively surprise. \"And it your first"
"2501"	"case! And you know perfectly well there never would have been any case"
"2502"	"if he had got that chance, don't you? And you'd have finished your days"
"2503"	"a pauper nobody, instead of being an actually launched and recognized"
"2504"	"lawyer to-day. And you would really have done that, would you?\""
"2505"	"\"Certainly.\""
"2506"	"Tom looked at him a moment or two, then shook his head sorrowfully and"
"2507"	"said--"
"2508"	"\"I believe you--upon my word I do. I don't know why I do, but I do."
"2509"	"Pudd'nhead Wilson, I think you're the biggest fool I ever saw.\""
"2510"	"\"Thank you.\""
"2511"	"\"Don't mention it.\""
"2512"	"\"Well, he has been requiring you to fight the Italian and you have"
"2513"	"refused. You degenerate remnant of an honorable line! I'm thoroughly"
"2514"	"ashamed of you, Tom!\""
"2515"	"\"Oh, that's nothing! I don't care for anything, now that the will's torn"
"2516"	"up again.\""
"2517"	"\"Tom, tell me squarely--didn't he find any fault with you for anything"
"2518"	"but those two things--carrying the case into court and refusing to"
"2519"	"fight?\""
"2520"	"He watched the young fellow's face narrowly, but it was entirely"
"2521"	"reposeful, and so also was the voice that answered:"
"2522"	"\"No, he didn't find any other fault with me. If he had had any to find,"
"2523"	"he would have begun yesterday, for he was just in the humor for it. He"
"2524"	"drove that jack-pair around town and showed them the sights, and when he"
"2525"	"came home he couldn't find his father's old silver watch that don't keep"
"2526"	"time and he thinks so much of, and couldn't remember what he did with it"
"2527"	"three or four days ago when he saw it last, and so when I arrived he was"
"2528"	"all in a sweat about it, and when I suggested that it probably wasn't"
"2529"	"lost but stolen, it put him in a regular passion and he said I was a"
"2530"	"fool--which convinced me, without any trouble, that that was just what"
"2531"	"he was afraid had happened, himself, but did not want to believe it,"
"2532"	"because lost things stand a better chance of being found again than"
"2533"	"stolen ones.\""
"2534"	"\"Whe-ew!\" whistled Wilson; \"score another on the list.\""
"2535"	"\"Another what?\""
"2536"	"\"Another theft!\""
"2537"	"\"Theft?\""
"2538"	"\"Yes, theft. That watch isn't lost, it's stolen. There's been another"
"2539"	"raid on the town--and just the same old mysterious sort of thing that"
"2540"	"has happened once before, as you remember.\""
"2541"	"\"You don't mean it!\""
"2542"	"\"It's as sure as you are born! Have you missed anything yourself?\""
"2543"	"\"No. That is, I did miss a silver pencil-case that Aunt Mary Pratt gave"
"2544"	"me last birthday--\""
"2545"	"\"You'll find it stolen--that's what you'll find.\""
"2546"	"\"No, I sha'n't; for when I suggested theft about the watch and got such"
"2547"	"a rap, I went and examined my room, and the pencil-case was missing, but"
"2548"	"it was only mislaid, and I found it again.\""
"2549"	"\"You are sure you missed nothing else?\""
"2550"	"\"Well, nothing of consequence. I missed a small plain gold ring worth"
"2551"	"two or three dollars, but that will turn up. I'll look again.\""
"2552"	"\"In my opinion you'll not find it. There's been a raid, I tell you. Come"
"2553"	"in!\""
"2554"	"Mr. Justice Robinson entered, followed by Buckstone and the"
"2555"	"town-constable, Jim Blake. They sat down, and after some wandering and"
"2556"	"aimless weather-conversation Wilson said--"
"2557"	"\"By the way, we've just added another to the list of thefts, maybe two."
"2558"	"Judge Driscoll's old silver watch is gone, and Tom here has missed a"
"2559"	"gold ring.\""
"2560"	"\"Well, it is a bad business,\" said the Justice, \"and gets worse the"
"2561"	"further it goes. The Hankses, the Dobsons, the Pilligrews, the Ortons,"
"2562"	"the Grangers, the Hales, the Fullers, the Holcombs, in fact everybody"
"2563"	"that lives around about Patsy Cooper's has been robbed of little things"
"2564"	"like trinkets and teaspoons and such-like small valuables that are"
"2565"	"easily carried off. It's perfectly plain that the thief took advantage"
"2566"	"of the reception at Patsy Cooper's when all the neighbors were in her"
"2567"	"house and all their niggers hanging around her fence for a look at the"
"2568"	"show, to raid the vacant houses undisturbed. Patsy is miserable about"
"2569"	"it; miserable on account of the neighbors, and particularly miserable on"
"2570"	"account of her foreigners, of course; so miserable on their account that"
"2571"	"she hasn't any room to worry about her own little losses.\""
"2572"	"\"It's the same old raider,\" said Wilson. \"I suppose there isn't any"
"2573"	"doubt about that.\""
"2574"	"\"Constable Blake doesn't think so.\""
"2575"	"\"No, you're wrong there,\" said Blake; \"the other times it was a man;"
"2576"	"there was plenty of signs of that, as we know, in the profession, though"
"2577"	"we never got hands on him; but this time it's a woman.\""
"2578"	"Wilson thought of the mysterious girl straight off. She was always in"
"2579"	"his mind now. But she failed him again. Blake continued:"
"2580"	"\"She's a stoop-shouldered old woman with a covered basket on her arm, in"
"2581"	"a black veil, dressed in mourning. I saw her going aboard the ferry-boat"
"2582"	"yesterday. Lives in Illinois, I reckon; but I don't care where she"
"2583"	"lives, I'm going to get her--she can make herself sure of that.\""
"2584"	"\"What makes you think she's the thief?\""
"2585"	"\"Well, there ain't any other, for one thing; and for another, some"
"2586"	"nigger draymen that happened to be driving along saw her coming out of"
"2587"	"or going into houses, and told me so--and it just happens that they was"
"2588"	"robbed houses, every time.\""
"2589"	"It was granted that this was plenty good enough circumstantial evidence."
"2590"	"A pensive silence followed, which lasted some moments, then Wilson"
"2591"	"said--"
"2592"	"\"There's one good thing, anyway. She can't either pawn or sell Count"
"2593"	"Luigi's costly Indian dagger.\""
"2594"	"\"My!\" said Tom, \"is that gone?\""
"2595"	"\"Yes.\""
"2596"	"\"Well, that was a haul! But why can't she pawn it or sell it?\""
"2597"	"\"Because when the twins went home from the Sons of Liberty meeting last"
"2598"	"night, news of the raid was sifting in from everywhere, and Aunt Patsy"
"2599"	"was in distress to know if they had lost anything. They found that the"
"2600"	"dagger was gone, and they notified the police and pawnbrokers"
"2601"	"everywhere. It was a great haul, yes, but the old woman won't get"
"2602"	"anything out of it, because she'll get caught.\""
"2603"	"\"Did they offer a reward?\" asked Buckstone."
"2604"	"\"Yes; five hundred dollars for the knife, and five hundred more for the"
"2605"	"thief.\""
"2606"	"\"What a leather-headed idea!\" exclaimed the constable. \"The thief"
"2607"	"da'sn't go near them, nor send anybody. Whoever goes is going to get"
"2608"	"himself nabbed, for their ain't any pawnbroker that's going to lose the"
"2609"	"chance to--\""
"2610"	"If anybody had noticed Tom's face at that time, the gray-green color of"
"2611"	"it might have provoked curiosity; but nobody did. He said to himself:"
"2612"	"\"I'm gone! I never can square up; the rest of the plunder won't pawn or"
"2613"	"sell for half of the bill. Oh, I know it--I'm gone, I'm gone--and this"
"2614"	"time it's for good. Oh, this is awful--I don't know what to do, nor"
"2615"	"which way to turn!\""
"2616"	"\"Softly, softly,\" said Wilson to Blake. \"I planned their scheme for them"
"2617"	"at midnight last night, and it was all finished up shipshape by two this"
"2618"	"morning. They'll get their dagger back, and then I'll explain to you how"
"2619"	"the thing was done.\""
"2620"	"There were strong signs of a general curiosity, and Buckstone said--"
"2621"	"\"Well, you have whetted us up pretty sharp, Wilson, and I'm free to say"
"2622"	"that if you don't mind telling us in confidence--\""
"2623"	"\"Oh, I'd as soon tell as not, Buckstone, but as long as the twins and I"
"2624"	"agreed to say nothing about it, we must let it stand so. But you can"
"2625"	"take my word for it you won't be kept waiting three days. Somebody will"
"2626"	"apply for that reward pretty promptly, and I'll show you the thief and"
"2627"	"the dagger both very soon afterward.\""
"2628"	"The constable was disappointed, and also perplexed. He said--"
"2629"	"\"It may all be--yes, and I hope it will, but I'm blamed if I can see my"
"2630"	"way through it. It's too many for yours truly.\""
"2631"	"The subject seemed about talked out. Nobody seemed to have anything"
"2632"	"further to offer. After a silence the justice of the peace informed"
"2633"	"Wilson that he and Buckstone and the constable had come as a committee,"
"2634"	"on the part of the Democratic party, to ask him to run for mayor--for"
"2635"	"the little town was about to become a city and the first charter"
"2636"	"election was approaching. It was the first attention which Wilson had"
"2637"	"ever received at the hands of any party; it was a sufficiently humble"
"2638"	"one, but it was a recognition of his début into the town's life and"
"2639"	"activities at last; it was a step upward, and he was deeply gratified."
"2640"	"He accepted, and the committee departed, followed by young Tom."
"2641"	"CHAPTER XIV."
"2642"	"Roxana Insists Upon Reform."
"2643"	"The true Southern watermelon is a boon apart, and not to be mentioned"
"2644"	"with commoner things. It is chief of this world's luxuries, king by the"
"2645"	"grace of God over all the fruits of the earth. When one has tasted it,"
"2646"	"he knows what the angels eat. It was not a Southern watermelon that Eve"
"2647"	"took: we know it because she repented.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"2648"	"About the time that Wilson was bowing the committee out, Pembroke Howard"
"2649"	"was entering the next house to report. He found the old Judge sitting"
"2650"	"grim and straight in his chair, waiting."
"2651"	"\"Well, Howard--the news?\""
"2652"	"\"The best in the world.\""
"2653"	"\"Accepts, does he?\" and the light of battle gleamed joyously in the"
"2654"	"Judge's eye."
"2655"	"\"Accepts? Why, he jumped at it.\""
"2656"	"\"Did, did he? Now that's fine--that's very fine. I like that. When is it"
"2657"	"to be?\""
"2658"	"\"Now! Straight off! To-night! An admirable fellow--admirable!\""
"2659"	"\"Admirable? He's a darling! Why, it's an honor as well as a pleasure to"
"2660"	"stand up before such a man. Come--off with you! Go and arrange"
"2661"	"everything--and give him my heartiest compliments. A rare fellow,"
"2662"	"indeed; an admirable fellow, as you have said!\""
"2663"	"Howard hurried away, saying--"
"2664"	"\"I'll have him in the vacant stretch between Wilson's and the haunted"
"2665"	"house within the hour, and I'll bring my own pistols.\""
"2666"	"Judge Driscoll began to walk the floor in a state of pleased excitement;"
"2667"	"but presently he stopped, and began to think--began to think of Tom."
"2668"	"Twice he moved toward the secretary, and twice he turned away again; but"
"2669"	"finally he said--"
"2670"	"\"This may be my last night in the world--I must not take the chance. He"
"2671"	"is worthless and unworthy, but it is largely my fault. He was intrusted"
"2672"	"to me by my brother on his dying bed, and I have indulged him to his"
"2673"	"hurt, instead of training him up severely, and making a man of him. I"
"2674"	"have violated my trust, and I must not add the sin of desertion to that."
"2675"	"I have forgiven him once already, and would subject him to a long and"
"2676"	"hard trial before forgiving him again, if I could live; but I must not"
"2677"	"run that risk. No, I must restore the will. But if I survive the duel, I"
"2678"	"will hide it away, and he will not know, and I will not tell him until"
"2679"	"he reforms, and I see that his reformation is going to be permanent.\""
"2680"	"He re-drew the will, and his ostensible nephew was heir to a fortune"
"2681"	"again. As he was finishing his task, Tom, wearied with another brooding"
"2682"	"tramp, entered the house and went tiptoeing past the sitting-room door."
"2683"	"He glanced in, and hurried on, for the sight of his uncle had nothing"
"2684"	"but terrors for him to-night. But his uncle was writing! That was"
"2685"	"unusual at this late hour. What could he be writing? A chill of anxiety"
"2686"	"settled down upon Tom's heart. Did that writing concern him? He was"
"2687"	"afraid so. He reflected that when ill luck begins, it does not come in"
"2688"	"sprinkles, but in showers. He said he would get a glimpse of that"
"2689"	"document or know the reason why. He heard some one coming, and stepped"
"2690"	"out of sight and hearing. It was Pembroke Howard. What could be"
"2691"	"hatching?"
"2692"	"Howard said, with great satisfaction:"
"2693"	"\"Everything's right and ready. He's gone to the battle-ground with his"
"2694"	"second and the surgeon--also with his brother. I've arranged it all with"
"2695"	"Wilson--Wilson's his second. We are to have three shots apiece.\""
"2696"	"\"Good! How is the moon?\""
"2697"	"\"Bright as day, nearly. Perfect, for the distance--fifteen yards. No"
"2698"	"wind--not a breath; hot and still.\""
"2699"	"\"All good; all first-rate. Here, Pembroke, read this, and witness it.\""
"2700"	"Pembroke read and witnessed the will, then gave the old man's hand a"
"2701"	"hearty shake and said:"
"2702"	"\"Now that's right, York--but I knew you would do it. You couldn't leave"
"2703"	"that poor chap to fight along without means or profession, with certain"
"2704"	"defeat before him, and I knew you wouldn't, for his father's sake if not"
"2705"	"for his own.\""
"2706"	"\"For his dead father's sake I couldn't, I know; for poor Percy--but you"
"2707"	"know what Percy was to me. But mind--Tom is not to know of this unless I"
"2708"	"fall to-night.\""
"2709"	"\"I understand. I'll keep the secret.\""
"2710"	"The Judge put the will away, and the two started for the battle-ground."
"2711"	"In another minute the will was in Tom's hands. His misery vanished, his"
"2712"	"feelings underwent a tremendous revulsion. He put the will carefully"
"2713"	"back in its place, and spread his mouth and swung his hat once, twice,"
"2714"	"three times around his head, in imitation of three rousing huzzas, no"
"2715"	"sound issuing from his lips. He fell to communing with himself excitedly"
"2716"	"and joyously, but every now and then he let off another volley of dumb"
"2717"	"hurrahs."
"2718"	"He said to himself: \"I've got the fortune again, but I'll not let on"
"2719"	"that I know about it. And this time I'm going to hang on to it. I take"
"2720"	"no more risks. I'll gamble no more, I'll drink no more, because--well,"
"2721"	"because I'll not go where there is any of that sort of thing going on,"
"2722"	"again. It's the sure way, and the only sure way; I might have thought of"
"2723"	"that sooner--well, yes, if I had wanted to. But now--dear me, I've had a"
"2724"	"scare this time, and I'll take no more chances. Not a single chance"
"2725"	"more. Land! I persuaded myself this evening that I could fetch him"
"2726"	"around without any great amount of effort, but I've been getting more"
"2727"	"and more heavy-hearted and doubtful straight along, ever since. If he"
"2728"	"tells me about this thing, all right; but if he doesn't, I sha'n't let"
"2729"	"on. I--well, I'd like to tell Pudd'nhead Wilson, but--no, I'll think"
"2730"	"about that; perhaps I won't.\" He whirled off another dead huzza, and"
"2731"	"said, \"I'm reformed, and this time I'll stay so, sure!\""
"2732"	"He was about to close with a final grand silent demonstration, when he"
"2733"	"suddenly recollected that Wilson had put it out of his power to pawn or"
"2734"	"sell the Indian knife, and that he was once more in awful peril of"
"2735"	"exposure by his creditors for that reason. His joy collapsed utterly,"
"2736"	"and he turned away and moped toward the door moaning and lamenting over"
"2737"	"the bitterness of his luck. He dragged himself up-stairs, and brooded in"
"2738"	"his room a long time disconsolate and forlorn, with Luigi's Indian knife"
"2739"	"for a text. At last he sighed and said:"
"2740"	"\"When I supposed these stones were glass and this ivory bone, the thing"
"2741"	"hadn't any interest for me because it hadn't any value, and couldn't"
"2742"	"help me out of my trouble. But now--why, now it is full of interest;"
"2743"	"yes, and of a sort to break a body's heart. It's a bag of gold that has"
"2744"	"turned to dirt and ashes in my hands. It could save me, and save me so"
"2745"	"easily, and yet I've got to go to ruin. It's like drowning with a"
"2746"	"life-preserver in my reach. All the hard luck comes to me, and all the"
"2747"	"good luck goes to other people--Pudd'nhead Wilson, for instance; even"
"2748"	"his career has got a sort of a little start at last, and what has he"
"2749"	"done to deserve it, I should like to know? Yes, he has opened his own"
"2750"	"road, but he isn't content with that, but must block mine. It's a"
"2751"	"sordid, selfish world, and I wish I was out of it.\" He allowed the light"
"2752"	"of the candle to play upon the jewels of the sheath, but the flashings"
"2753"	"and sparklings had no charm for his eye; they were only just so many"
"2754"	"pangs to his heart. \"I must not say anything to Roxy about this thing,\""
"2755"	"he said, \"she is too daring. She would be for digging these stones out"
"2756"	"and selling them, and then--why, she would be arrested and the stones"
"2757"	"traced, and then--\" The thought made him quake, and he hid the knife"
"2758"	"away, trembling all over and glancing furtively about, like a criminal"
"2759"	"who fancies that the accuser is already at hand."
"2760"	"Should he try to sleep? Oh, no, sleep was not for him; his trouble was"
"2761"	"too haunting, too afflicting for that. He must have somebody to mourn"
"2762"	"with. He would carry his despair to Roxy."
"2763"	"He had heard several distant gunshots, but that sort of thing was not"
"2764"	"uncommon, and they had made no impression upon him. He went out at the"
"2765"	"back door, and turned westward. He passed Wilson's house and proceeded"
"2766"	"along the lane, and presently saw several figures approaching Wilson's"
"2767"	"place through the vacant lots. These were the duelists returning from"
"2768"	"the fight; he thought he recognized them, but as he had no desire for"
"2769"	"white people's company, he stooped down behind the fence until they were"
"2770"	"out of his way."
"2771"	"Roxy was feeling fine. She said:"
"2772"	"\"Whah was you, child? Warn't you in it?\""
"2773"	"\"In what?\""
"2774"	"\"In de duel.\""
"2775"	"\"Duel? Has there been a duel?\""
"2776"	"\"'Co'se dey has. De ole Jedge has be'n havin' a duel wid one o' dem"
"2777"	"twins.\""
"2778"	"\"Great Scott!\" Then he added to himself: \"That's what made him re-make"
"2779"	"the will; he thought he might get killed, and it softened him toward me."
"2780"	"And that's what he and Howard were so busy about.... Oh dear, if the"
"2781"	"twin had only killed him, I should be out of my--\""
"2782"	"\"What is you mumblin' bout, Chambers? Whah was you? Didn't you know dey"
"2783"	"was gwyne to be a duel?\""
"2784"	"\"No, I didn't. The old man tried to get me to fight one with Count"
"2785"	"Luigi, but he didn't succeed, so I reckon he concluded to patch up the"
"2786"	"family honor himself.\""
"2787"	"He laughed at the idea, and went rambling on with a detailed account of"
"2788"	"his talk with the Judge, and how shocked and ashamed the Judge was to"
"2789"	"find that he had a coward in his family. He glanced up at last, and got"
"2790"	"a shock himself. Roxana's bosom was heaving with suppressed passion, and"
"2791"	"she was glowering down upon him with measureless contempt written in her"
"2792"	"face."
"2793"	"\"En you refuse' to fight a man dat kicked you, 'stid o' jumpin' at de"
"2794"	"chance! En you ain't got no mo' feelin' den to come en tell me, dat"
"2795"	"fetched sich a po' low-down ornery rabbit into de worl'! Pah! it make me"
"2796"	"sick! It's de nigger in you, dat's what it is. Thirty-one parts o' you"
"2797"	"is white, en on'y one part nigger, en dat po' little one part is yo'"
"2798"	"soul. Tain't wuth savin'; tain't wuth totin' out on a shovel en throwin'"
"2799"	"in de gutter. You has disgraced yo' birth. What would yo' pa think o'"
"2800"	"you? It's enough to make him turn in his grave.\""
"2801"	"The last three sentences stung Tom into a fury, and he said to himself"
"2802"	"that if his father were only alive and in reach of assassination his"
"2803"	"mother would soon find that he had a very clear notion of the size of"
"2804"	"his indebtedness to that man, and was willing to pay it up in full, and"
"2805"	"would do it too, even at risk of his life; but he kept this thought to"
"2806"	"himself; that was safest in his mother's present state."
"2807"	"\"Whatever has come o' yo' Essex blood? Dat's what I can't understan'. En"
"2808"	"it ain't on'y jist Essex blood dat's in you, not by a long sight--'deed"
"2809"	"it ain't! My great-great-great-gran'father en yo'"
"2810"	"great-great-great-great-gran'father was Ole Cap'n John Smith, de highest"
"2811"	"blood dat Ole Virginny ever turned out, en his great-great-gran'mother"
"2812"	"or somers along back dah, was Pocahontas de Injun queen, en her husbun'"
"2813"	"was a nigger king outen Africa--en yit here you is, a slinkin' outen a"
"2814"	"duel en disgracin' our whole line like a ornery low-down hound! Yes,"
"2815"	"it's de nigger in you!\""
"2816"	"She sat down on her candle-box and fell into a reverie. Tom did not"
"2817"	"disturb her; he sometimes lacked prudence, but it was not in"
"2818"	"circumstances of this kind, Roxana's storm went gradually down, but it"
"2819"	"died hard, and even when it seemed to be quite gone, it would now and"
"2820"	"then break out in a distant rumble, so to speak, in the form of muttered"
"2821"	"ejaculations. One of these was, \"Ain't nigger enough in him to show in"
"2822"	"his finger-nails, en dat takes mighty little--yit dey's enough to paint"
"2823"	"his soul.\""
"2824"	"Presently she muttered. \"Yassir, enough to paint a whole thimbleful of"
"2825"	"'em.\" At last her ramblings ceased altogether, and her countenance began"
"2826"	"to clear--a welcome sign to Tom, who had learned her moods, and knew she"
"2827"	"was on the threshold of good-humor, now. He noticed that from time to"
"2828"	"time she unconsciously carried her finger to the end of her nose. He"
"2829"	"looked closer and said:"
"2830"	"\"Why, mammy, the end of your nose is skinned. How did that come?\""
"2831"	"She sent out the sort of whole-hearted peal of laughter which God had"
"2832"	"vouchsafed in its perfection to none but the happy angels in heaven and"
"2833"	"the bruised and broken black slave on the earth, and said:"
"2834"	"\"Dad fetch dat duel, I be'n in it myself.\""
"2835"	"\"Gracious! did a bullet do that?\""
"2836"	"\"Yassir, you bet it did!\""
"2837"	"\"Well, I declare! Why, how did that happen?\""
"2838"	"\"Happened dis-away. I 'uz a-sett'n' here kinder dozin' in de dark, en"
"2839"	"che-bang! goes a gun, right out dah. I skips along out towards t'other"
"2840"	"end o' de house to see what's gwyne on, en stops by de ole winder on de"
"2841"	"side towards Pudd'nhead Wilson's house dat ain't got no sash in it,--but"
"2842"	"dey ain't none of 'em got any sashes, fur as dat's concerned,--en I"
"2843"	"stood dah in de dark en look out, en dar in de moonlight, right down"
"2844"	"under me 'uz one o' de twins a-cussin'--not much, but jist a-cussin'"
"2845"	"soft--it 'uz de brown one dat 'uz cussin', 'ca'se he 'uz hit in de"
"2846"	"shoulder. En Doctor Claypool he 'uz a-workin' at him, en Pudd'nhead"
"2847"	"Wilson he 'uz a-he'pin', en ole Jedge Driscoll en Pem Howard 'uz"
"2848"	"a-standin' out yonder a little piece waitin' for 'em to git ready agin."
"2849"	"En treckly dey squared off en give de word, en bang-bang went de"
"2850"	"pistols, en de twin he say, 'Ouch!'--hit him on de han' dis time,--en I"
"2851"	"hear dat same bullet go spat! ag'in, de logs under de winder; en de nex'"
"2852"	"time dey shoot, de twin say, 'Ouch!' ag'in, en I done it too, 'ca'se de"
"2853"	"bullet glance' on his cheek-bone en skip up here en glance on de side o'"
"2854"	"de winder en whiz right acrost my face en tuck de hide off'n my"
"2855"	"nose--why, if I'd 'a' be'n jist a inch or a inch en a half furder 't"
"2856"	"would 'a' tuck de whole nose en disfiggered me. Here's de bullet; I"
"2857"	"hunted her up.\""
"2858"	"\"Did you stand there all the time?\""
"2859"	"\"Dat's a question to ask, ain't it? What else would I do? Does I git a"
"2860"	"chance to see a duel every day?\""
"2861"	"\"Why, you were right in range! Weren't you afraid?\""
"2862"	"The woman gave a sniff of scorn."
"2863"	"\"'Fraid! De Smith-Pocahontases ain't 'fraid o' nothin', let alone"
"2864"	"bullets.\""
"2865"	"\"They've got pluck enough, I suppose; what they lack is judgment. I"
"2866"	"wouldn't have stood there.\""
"2867"	"\"Nobody's accusin' you!\""
"2868"	"\"Did anybody else get hurt?\""
"2869"	"\"Yes, we all got hit 'cep' de blon' twin en de doctor en de seconds. De"
"2870"	"Jedge didn't git hurt, but I hear Pudd'nhead say de bullet snip some o'"
"2871"	"his ha'r off.\""
"2872"	"\"'George!\" said Tom to himself, \"to come so near being out of my"
"2873"	"trouble, and miss it by an inch. Oh dear, dear, he will live to find me"
"2874"	"out and sell me to some nigger-trader yet--yes, and he would do it in a"
"2875"	"minute.\" Then he said aloud, in a grave tone--"
"2876"	"\"Mother, we are in an awful fix.\""
"2877"	"Roxana caught her breath with a spasm, and said--"
"2878"	"\"Chile! What you hit a body so sudden for, like dat? What's be'n en gone"
"2879"	"en happen'?\""
"2880"	"\"Well, there's one thing I didn't tell you. When I wouldn't fight, he"
"2881"	"tore up the will again, and--\""
"2882"	"Roxana's face turned a dead white, and she said--"
"2883"	"\"Now you's done!--done forever! Dat's de end. Bofe un us is gwyne to"
"2884"	"starve to--\""
"2885"	"\"Wait and hear me through, can't you! I reckon that when he resolved to"
"2886"	"fight, himself, he thought he might get killed and not have a chance to"
"2887"	"forgive me any more in this life, so he made the will again, and I've"
"2888"	"seen it, and it's all right. But--\""
"2889"	"\"Oh, thank goodness, den we's safe ag'in!--safe! en so what did you want"
"2890"	"to come here en talk sich dreadful--\""
"2891"	"\"Hold on, I tell you, and let me finish. The swag I gathered won't half"
"2892"	"square me up, and the first thing we know, my creditors--well, you know"
"2893"	"what'll happen.\""
"2894"	"Roxana dropped her chin, and told her son to leave her alone--she must"
"2895"	"think this matter out. Presently she said impressively:"
"2896"	"\"You got to go mighty keerful now, I tell you! En here's what you got to"
"2897"	"do. He didn't git killed, en if you gives him de least reason, he'll"
"2898"	"bust de will ag'in, en dat's de las' time, now you hear me! So--you's"
"2899"	"got to show him what you kin do in de nex' few days. You's got to be"
"2900"	"pison good, en let him see it; you got to do everything dat'll make him"
"2901"	"b'lieve in you, en you got to sweeten aroun' ole Aunt Pratt, too,--she's"
"2902"	"pow'ful strong wid de Jedge, en de bes' frien' you got. Nex', you'll go"
"2903"	"'long away to Sent Louis, en dat'll keep him in yo' favor. Den you go en"
"2904"	"make a bargain wid dem people. You tell 'em he ain't gwyne to live"
"2905"	"long--en dat's de fac', too,--en tell 'em you'll pay 'em intrust, en big"
"2906"	"intrust, too,--ten per--what you call it?\""
"2907"	"\"Ten per cent. a month?\""
"2908"	"\"Dat's it. Den you take and sell yo' truck aroun', a little at a time,"
"2909"	"en pay de intrust. How long will it las'?\""
"2910"	"\"I think there's enough to pay the interest five or six months.\""
"2911"	"\"Den you's all right. If he don't die in six months, dat don't make no"
"2912"	"diff'rence--Providence'll provide. You's gwyne to be safe--if you"
"2913"	"behaves.\" She bent an austere eye on him and added, \"En you is gwyne to"
"2914"	"behave--does you know dat?\""
"2915"	"He laughed and said he was going to try, anyway. She did not unbend. She"
"2916"	"said gravely:"
"2917"	"\"Tryin' ain't de thing. You's gwyne to do it. You ain't gwyne to steal a"
"2918"	"pin--'ca'se it ain't safe no mo'; en you ain't gwyne into no bad"
"2919"	"comp'ny--not even once, you understand; en you ain't gwyne to drink a"
"2920"	"drop--nary single drop; en you ain't gwyne to gamble one single"
"2921"	"gamble--not one! Dis ain't what you's gwyne to try to do, it's what"
"2922"	"you's gwyne to do. En I'll tell you how I knows it. Dis is how. I's"
"2923"	"gwyne to foller along to Sent Louis my own self; en you's gwyne to come"
"2924"	"to me every day o' yo' life, en I'll look you over; en if you fails in"
"2925"	"one single one o' dem things--jist one--I take my oath I'll come"
"2926"	"straight down to dis town en tell de Jedge you's a nigger en a slave--en"
"2927"	"prove it!\" She paused to let her words sink home. Then she added,"
"2928"	"\"Chambers, does you b'lieve me when I says dat?\""
"2929"	"Tom was sober enough now. There was no levity in his voice when he"
"2930"	"answered:"
"2931"	"\"Yes, mother, I know, now, that I am reformed--and permanently."
"2932"	"Permanently--and beyond the reach of any human temptation.\""
"2933"	"\"Den g' long home en begin!\""
"2934"	"CHAPTER XV."
"2935"	"The Robber Robbed."
"2936"	"Nothing so needs reforming as other people's habits.--Pudd'nhead"
"2937"	"Wilson's Calendar."
"2938"	"Behold, the fool saith, \"Put not all thine eggs in the one"
"2939"	"basket\"--which is but a manner of saying, \"Scatter your money and your"
"2940"	"attention;\" but the wise man saith, \"Put all your eggs in the one basket"
"2941"	"and--watch that basket\"--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"2942"	"What a time of it Dawson's Landing was having! All its life it had been"
"2943"	"asleep, but now it hardly got a chance for a nod, so swiftly did big"
"2944"	"events and crashing surprises come along in one another's wake: Friday"
"2945"	"morning, first glimpse of Real Nobility, also grand reception at Aunt"
"2946"	"Patsy Cooper's, also great robber-raid; Friday evening, dramatic kicking"
"2947"	"of the heir of the chief citizen in presence of four hundred people;"
"2948"	"Saturday morning, emergence as practising lawyer of the long-submerged"
"2949"	"Pudd'nhead Wilson; Saturday night, duel between chief citizen and titled"
"2950"	"stranger."
"2951"	"The people took more pride in the duel than in all the other events put"
"2952"	"together, perhaps. It was a glory to their town to have such a thing"
"2953"	"happen there. In their eyes the principals had reached the summit of"
"2954"	"human honor. Everybody paid homage to their names; their praises were in"
"2955"	"all mouths. Even the duelists' subordinates came in for a handsome share"
"2956"	"of the public approbation: wherefore Pudd'nhead Wilson was suddenly"
"2957"	"become a man of consequence. When asked to run for the mayoralty"
"2958"	"Saturday night he was risking defeat, but Sunday morning found him a"
"2959"	"made man and his success assured."
"2960"	"The twins were prodigiously great, now; the town took them to its bosom"
"2961"	"with enthusiasm. Day after day, and night after night, they went dining"
"2962"	"and visiting from house to house, making friends, enlarging and"
"2963"	"solidifying their popularity, and charming and surprising all with their"
"2964"	"musical prodigies, and now and then heightening the effects with samples"
"2965"	"of what they could do in other directions, out of their stock of rare"
"2966"	"and curious accomplishments. They were so pleased that they gave the"
"2967"	"regulation thirty days' notice, the required preparation for"
"2968"	"citizenship, and resolved to finish their days in this pleasant place."
"2969"	"That was the climax. The delighted community rose as one man and"
"2970"	"applauded; and when the twins were asked to stand for seats in the"
"2971"	"forthcoming aldermanic board, and consented, the public contentment was"
"2972"	"rounded and complete."
"2973"	"Tom Driscoll was not happy over these things; they sunk deep, and hurt"
"2974"	"all the way down. He hated the one twin for kicking him, and the other"
"2975"	"one for being the kicker's brother."
"2976"	"Now and then the people wondered why nothing was heard of the raider, or"
"2977"	"of the stolen knife or the other plunder, but nobody was able to throw"
"2978"	"any light on that matter. Nearly a week had drifted by, and still the"
"2979"	"thing remained a vexed mystery."
"2980"	"On Saturday Constable Blake and Pudd'nhead Wilson met on the street, and"
"2981"	"Tom Driscoll joined them in time to open their conversation for them. He"
"2982"	"said to Blake--\"You are not looking well, Blake; you seem to be annoyed"
"2983"	"about something. Has anything gone wrong in the detective business? I"
"2984"	"believe you fairly and justifiably claim to have a pretty good"
"2985"	"reputation in that line, isn't it so?\"--which made Blake feel good, and"
"2986"	"look it; but Tom added, \"for a country detective\"--which made Blake feel"
"2987"	"the other way, and not only look it, but betray it in his voice--"
"2988"	"\"Yes, sir, I have got a reputation; and it's as good as anybody's in the"
"2989"	"profession, too, country or no country.\""
"2990"	"\"Oh, I beg pardon; I didn't mean any offense. What I started out to ask"
"2991"	"was only about the old woman that raided the town--the stoop-shouldered"
"2992"	"old woman, you know, that you said you were going to catch; and I knew"
"2993"	"you would, too, because you have the reputation of never boasting,"
"2994"	"and--well, you--you've caught the old woman?\""
"2995"	"\"D------ the old woman!\""
"2996"	"\"Why, sho! you don't mean to say you haven't caught her?\""
"2997"	"\"No; I haven't caught her. If anybody could have caught her, I could;"
"2998"	"but nobody couldn't, I don't care who he is.\""
"2999"	"\"I am sorry, real sorry--for your sake; because, when it gets around"
"3000"	"that a detective has expressed himself so confidently, and then--\""
"3001"	"\"Don't you worry, that's all--don't you worry; and as for the town, the"
"3002"	"town needn't worry, either. She's my meat--make yourself easy about"
"3003"	"that. I'm on her track; I've got clues that--\""
"3004"	"\"That's good! Now if you could get an old veteran detective down from"
"3005"	"St. Louis to help you find out what the clues mean, and where they lead"
"3006"	"to, and then--\""
"3007"	"\"I'm plenty veteran enough myself, and I don't need anybody's help. I'll"
"3008"	"have her inside of a we--inside of a month. That I'll swear to!\""
"3009"	"Tom said carelessly--"
"3010"	"\"I suppose that will answer--yes, that will answer. But I reckon she is"
"3011"	"pretty old, and old people don't often outlive the cautious pace of the"
"3012"	"professional detective when he has got his clues together and is out on"
"3013"	"his still-hunt.\""
"3014"	"Blake's dull face flushed under this gibe, but before he could set his"
"3015"	"retort in order Tom had turned to Wilson, and was saying, with placid"
"3016"	"indifference of manner and voice--"
"3017"	"\"Who got the reward, Pudd'nhead?\""
"3018"	"Wilson winced slightly, and saw that his own turn was come."
"3019"	"\"What reward?\""
"3020"	"\"Why, the reward for the thief, and the other one for the knife.\""
"3021"	"Wilson answered--and rather uncomfortably, to judge by his hesitating"
"3022"	"fashion of delivering himself--"
"3023"	"\"Well, the--well, in fact, nobody has claimed it yet.\""
"3024"	"Tom seemed surprised."
"3025"	"\"Why, is that so?\""
"3026"	"Wilson showed a trifle of irritation when he replied--"
"3027"	"\"Yes, it's so. And what of it?\""
"3028"	"\"Oh, nothing. Only I thought you had struck out a new idea, and invented"
"3029"	"a scheme that was going to revolutionize the time-worn and ineffectual"
"3030"	"methods of the--\" He stopped, and turned to Blake, who was happy now"
"3031"	"that another had taken his place on the gridiron: \"Blake, didn't you"
"3032"	"understand him to intimate that it wouldn't be necessary for you to hunt"
"3033"	"the old woman down?\""
"3034"	"\"B'George, he said he'd have thief and swag both inside of three"
"3035"	"days--he did, by hokey! and that's just about a week ago. Why, I said at"
"3036"	"the time that no thief and no thief's pal was going to try to pawn or"
"3037"	"sell a thing where he knowed the pawnbroker could get both rewards by"
"3038"	"taking him into camp with the swag. It was the blessedest idea that ever"
"3039"	"I struck!\""
"3040"	"\"You'd change your mind,\" said Wilson, with irritated bluntness, \"if you"
"3041"	"knew the entire scheme instead of only part of it.\""
"3042"	"\"Well,\" said the constable, pensively, \"I had the idea that it wouldn't"
"3043"	"work, and up to now I'm right anyway.\""
"3044"	"\"Very well, then, let it stand at that, and give it a further show. It"
"3045"	"has worked at least as well as your own methods, you perceive.\""
"3046"	"The constable hadn't anything handy to hit back with, so he discharged a"
"3047"	"discontented sniff, and said nothing."
"3048"	"After the night that Wilson had partly revealed his scheme at his house,"
"3049"	"Tom had tried for several days to guess out the secret of the rest of"
"3050"	"it, but had failed. Then it occurred to him to give Roxana's smarter"
"3051"	"head a chance at it. He made up a supposititious case, and laid it"
"3052"	"before her. She thought it over, and delivered her verdict upon it. Tom"
"3053"	"said to himself, \"She's hit it, sure!\" He thought he would test that"
"3054"	"verdict, now, and watch Wilson's face; so he said reflectively--"
"3055"	"\"Wilson, you're not a fool--a fact of recent discovery. Whatever your"
"3056"	"scheme was, it had sense in it, Blake's opinion to the contrary"
"3057"	"notwithstanding. I don't ask you to reveal it, but I will suppose a"
"3058"	"case--a case which will answer as a starting-point for the real thing I"
"3059"	"am going to come at, and that's all I want. You offered five hundred"
"3060"	"dollars for the knife, and five hundred for the thief. We will suppose,"
"3061"	"for argument's sake, that the first reward is advertised and the second"
"3062"	"offered by private letter to pawnbrokers and--\""
"3063"	"Blake slapped his thigh, and cried out--"
"3064"	"\"By Jackson, he's got you, Pudd'nhead! Now why couldn't I or any fool"
"3065"	"have thought of that?\""
"3066"	"Wilson said to himself, \"Anybody with a reasonably good head would have"
"3067"	"thought of it. I am not surprised that Blake didn't detect it; I am only"
"3068"	"surprised that Tom did. There is more to him than I supposed.\" He said"
"3069"	"nothing aloud, and Tom went on:"
"3070"	"\"Very well. The thief would not suspect that there was a trap, and he"
"3071"	"would bring or send the knife, and say he bought it for a song, or found"
"3072"	"it in the road, or something like that, and try to collect the reward,"
"3073"	"and be arrested--wouldn't he?\""
"3074"	"\"Yes,\" said Wilson."
"3075"	"\"I think so,\" said Tom. \"There can't be any doubt of it. Have you ever"
"3076"	"seen that knife?\""
"3077"	"\"No.\""
"3078"	"\"Has any friend of yours?\""
"3079"	"\"Not that I know of.\""
"3080"	"\"Well, I begin to think I understand why your scheme failed.\""
"3081"	"\"What do you mean, Tom? What are you driving at?\" asked Wilson, with a"
"3082"	"dawning sense of discomfort."
"3083"	"\"Why, that there isn't any such knife.\""
"3084"	"\"Look here, Wilson,\" said Blake, \"Tom Driscoll's right, for a thousand"
"3085"	"dollars--if I had it.\""
"3086"	"Wilson's blood warmed a little, and he wondered if he had been played"
"3087"	"upon by those strangers; it certainly had something of that look. But"
"3088"	"what could they gain by it? He threw out that suggestion. Tom replied:"
"3089"	"\"Gain? Oh, nothing that you would value, maybe. But they are strangers"
"3090"	"making their way in a new community. Is it nothing to them to appear as"
"3091"	"pets of an Oriental prince--at no expense? Is it nothing to them to be"
"3092"	"able to dazzle this poor little town with thousand-dollar rewards--at no"
"3093"	"expense? Wilson, there isn't any such knife, or your scheme would have"
"3094"	"fetched it to light. Or if there is any such knife, they've got it yet."
"3095"	"I believe, myself, that they've seen such a knife, for Angelo pictured"
"3096"	"it out with his pencil too swiftly and handily for him to have been"
"3097"	"inventing it, and of course I can't swear that they've never had it; but"
"3098"	"this I'll go bail for--if they had it when they came to this town,"
"3099"	"they've got it yet.\""
"3100"	"Blake said--"
"3101"	"\"It looks mighty reasonable, the way Tom puts it; it most certainly"
"3102"	"does.\""
"3103"	"Tom responded, turning to leave--"
"3104"	"\"You find the old woman, Blake, and if she can't furnish the knife, go"
"3105"	"and search the twins!\""
"3106"	"Tom sauntered away. Wilson felt a good deal depressed. He hardly knew"
"3107"	"what to think. He was loath to withdraw his faith from the twins, and"
"3108"	"was resolved not to do it on the present indecisive evidence; but--well,"
"3109"	"he would think, and then decide how to act."
"3110"	"\"Blake, what do you think of this matter?\""
"3111"	"\"Well, Pudd'nhead, I'm bound to say I put it up the way Tom does. They"
"3112"	"hadn't the knife; or if they had it, they've got it yet.\""
"3113"	"The men parted. Wilson said to himself:"
"3114"	"\"I believe they had it; if it had been stolen, the scheme would have"
"3115"	"restored it, that is certain. And so I believe they've got it yet.\""
"3116"	"Tom had no purpose in his mind when he encountered those two men. When"
"3117"	"he began his talk he hoped to be able to gall them a little and get a"
"3118"	"trifle of malicious entertainment out of it. But when he left, he left"
"3119"	"in great spirits, for he perceived that just by pure luck and no"
"3120"	"troublesome labor he had accomplished several delightful things: he had"
"3121"	"touched both men on a raw spot and seen them squirm; he had modified"
"3122"	"Wilson's sweetness for the twins with one small bitter taste that he"
"3123"	"wouldn't be able to get out of his mouth right away; and, best of all,"
"3124"	"he had taken the hated twins down a peg with the community; for Blake"
"3125"	"would gossip around freely, after the manner of detectives, and within a"
"3126"	"week the town would be laughing at them in its sleeve for offering a"
"3127"	"gaudy reward for a bauble which they either never possessed or hadn't"
"3128"	"lost. Tom was very well satisfied with himself."
"3129"	"Tom's behavior at home had been perfect during the entire week. His"
"3130"	"uncle and aunt had seen nothing like it before. They could find no fault"
"3131"	"with him anywhere."
"3132"	"Saturday evening he said to the Judge--"
"3133"	"\"I've had something preying on my mind, uncle, and as I am going away,"
"3134"	"and might never see you again, I can't bear it any longer. I made you"
"3135"	"believe I was afraid to fight that Italian adventurer. I had to get out"
"3136"	"of it on some pretext or other, and maybe I chose badly, being taken"
"3137"	"unawares, but no honorable person could consent to meet him in the"
"3138"	"field, knowing what I knew about him.\""
"3139"	"\"Indeed? What was that?\""
"3140"	"\"Count Luigi is a confessed assassin.\""
"3141"	"\"Incredible!\""
"3142"	"\"It's perfectly true. Wilson detected it in his hand, by palmistry, and"
"3143"	"charged him with it, and cornered him up so close that he had to"
"3144"	"confess; but both twins begged us on their knees to keep the secret, and"
"3145"	"swore they would lead straight lives here; and it was all so pitiful"
"3146"	"that we gave our word of honor never to expose them while they kept that"
"3147"	"promise. You would have done it yourself, uncle.\""
"3148"	"\"You are right, my boy; I would. A man's secret is still his own"
"3149"	"property, and sacred, when it has been surprised out of him like that."
"3150"	"You did well, and I am proud of you.\" Then he added mournfully, \"But I"
"3151"	"wish I could have been saved the shame of meeting an assassin on the"
"3152"	"field of honor.\""
"3153"	"\"It couldn't be helped, uncle. If I had known you were going to"
"3154"	"challenge him I should have felt obliged to sacrifice my pledged word in"
"3155"	"order to stop it, but Wilson couldn't be expected to do otherwise than"
"3156"	"keep silent.\""
"3157"	"\"Oh, no; Wilson did right, and is in no way to blame. Tom, Tom, you have"
"3158"	"lifted a heavy load from my heart; I was stung to the very soul when I"
"3159"	"seemed to have discovered that I had a coward in my family.\""
"3160"	"\"You may imagine what it cost me to assume such a part, uncle.\""
"3161"	"\"Oh, I know it, poor boy, I know it. And I can understand how much it"
"3162"	"has cost you to remain under that unjust stigma to this time. But it is"
"3163"	"all right now, and no harm is done. You have restored my comfort of"
"3164"	"mind, and with it your own; and both of us had suffered enough.\""
"3165"	"The old man sat awhile plunged in thought; then he looked up with a"
"3166"	"satisfied light in his eye, and said: \"That this assassin should have"
"3167"	"put the affront upon me of letting me meet him on the field of honor as"
"3168"	"if he were a gentleman is a matter which I will presently settle--but"
"3169"	"not now. I will not shoot him until after election. I see a way to ruin"
"3170"	"them both before; I will attend to that first. Neither of them shall be"
"3171"	"elected, that I promise. You are sure that the fact that he is an"
"3172"	"assassin has not got abroad?\""
"3173"	"\"Perfectly certain of it, sir.\""
"3174"	"\"It will be a good card. I will fling a hint at it from the stump on the"
"3175"	"polling-day. It will sweep the ground from under both of them.\""
"3176"	"\"There's not a doubt of it. It will finish them.\""
"3177"	"\"That and outside work among the voters will, to a certainty. I want you"
"3178"	"to come down here by and by and work privately among the rag-tag and"
"3179"	"bobtail. You shall spend money among them; I will furnish it.\""
"3180"	"Another point scored against the detested twins! Really it was a great"
"3181"	"day for Tom. He was encouraged to chance a parting shot, now, at the"
"3182"	"same target, and did it."
"3183"	"\"You know that wonderful Indian knife that the twins have been making"
"3184"	"such a to-do about? Well, there's no track or trace of it yet; so the"
"3185"	"town is beginning to sneer and gossip and laugh. Half the people believe"
"3186"	"they never had any such knife, the other half believe they had it and"
"3187"	"have got it still. I've heard twenty people talking like that to-day.\""
"3188"	"Yes, Tom's blemishless week had restored him to the favor of his aunt"
"3189"	"and uncle."
"3190"	"His mother was satisfied with him, too. Privately, she believed she was"
"3191"	"coming to love him, but she did not say so. She told him to go along to"
"3192"	"St. Louis, now, and she would get ready and follow. Then she smashed her"
"3193"	"whisky bottle and said--"
"3194"	"\"Dah now! I's a-gwyne to make you walk as straight as a string,"
"3195"	"Chambers, en so I's bown' you ain't gwyne to git no bad example out o'"
"3196"	"yo' mammy. I tole you you couldn't go into no bad comp'ny. Well, you's"
"3197"	"gwyne into my comp'ny, en I's gwyne to fill de bill. Now, den, trot"
"3198"	"along, trot along!\""
"3199"	"Tom went aboard one of the big transient boats that night with his heavy"
"3200"	"satchel of miscellaneous plunder, and slept the sleep of the unjust,"
"3201"	"which is serener and sounder than the other kind, as we know by the"
"3202"	"hanging-eve history of a million rascals. But when he got up in the"
"3203"	"morning, luck was against him again: A brother-thief had robbed him"
"3204"	"while he slept, and gone ashore at some intermediate landing."
"3205"	"CHAPTER XVI."
"3206"	"Sold Down the River."
"3207"	"If you pick up a starving dog and make him prosperous, he will not bite"
"3208"	"you. This is the principal difference between a dog and a"
"3209"	"man.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"3210"	"We know all about the habits of the ant, we know all about the habits of"
"3211"	"the bee, but we know nothing at all about the habits of the oyster. It"
"3212"	"seems almost certain that we have been choosing the wrong time for"
"3213"	"studying the oyster.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"3214"	"When Roxana arrived, she found her son in such despair and misery that"
"3215"	"her heart was touched and her motherhood rose up strong in her. He was"
"3216"	"ruined past hope, now; his destruction would be immediate and sure, and"
"3217"	"he would be an outcast and friendless. That was reason enough for a"
"3218"	"mother to love a child; so she loved him, and told him so. It made him"
"3219"	"wince, secretly--for she was a \"nigger.\" That he was one himself was far"
"3220"	"from reconciling him to that despised race."
"3221"	"Roxana poured out endearments upon him, to which he responded"
"3222"	"uncomfortably, but as well as he could. And she tried to comfort him,"
"3223"	"but that was not possible. These intimacies quickly became horrible to"
"3224"	"him, and within the hour he began to try to get up courage enough to"
"3225"	"tell her so, and require that they be discontinued or very considerably"
"3226"	"modified. But he was afraid of her; and besides, there came a lull, now,"
"3227"	"for she had begun to think. She was trying to invent a saving plan."
"3228"	"Finally she started up, and said she had found a way out. Tom was almost"
"3229"	"suffocated by the joy of this sudden good news. Roxana said:"
"3230"	"\"Here is de plan, en she'll win, sure. I's a nigger, en nobody ain't"
"3231"	"gwyne to doubt it dat hears me talk. I's wuth six hund'd dollahs. Take"
"3232"	"en sell me, en pay off dese gamblers.\""
"3233"	"Tom was dazed. He was not sure he had heard aright. He was dumb for a"
"3234"	"moment; then he said:"
"3235"	"\"Do you mean that you would be sold into slavery to save me?\""
"3236"	"\"Ain't you my chile? En does you know anything dat a mother won't do for"
"3237"	"her chile? Day ain't nothin' a white mother won't do for her chile. Who"
"3238"	"made 'em so? De Lord done it. En who made de niggers? De Lord made 'em."
"3239"	"In de inside, mothers is all de same. De good Lord he made 'em so. I's"
"3240"	"gwyne to be sole into slavery, en in a year you's gwyne to buy yo' ole"
"3241"	"mammy free ag'in. I'll show you how. Dat's de plan.\""
"3242"	"Tom's hopes began to rise, and his spirits along with them. He said--"
"3243"	"\"It's lovely of you, mammy--it's just--\""
"3244"	"\"Say it ag'in! En keep on sayin' it! It's all de pay a body kin want in"
"3245"	"dis worl', en it's mo' den enough. Laws bless you, honey, when I's"
"3246"	"slavin' aroun', en dey 'buses me, if I knows you's a-sayin' dat, 'way"
"3247"	"off yonder somers, it'll heal up all de sore places, en I kin stan'"
"3248"	"'em.\""
"3249"	"\"I do say it again, mammy, and I'll keep on saying it, too. But how am I"
"3250"	"going to sell you? You're free, you know.\""
"3251"	"\"Much diff'rence dat make! White folks ain't partic'lar. De law kin sell"
"3252"	"me now if dey tell me to leave de State in six months en I don't go. You"
"3253"	"draw up a paper--bill o' sale--en put it 'way off yonder, down in de"
"3254"	"middle o' Kaintuck somers, en sign some names to it, en say you'll sell"
"3255"	"me cheap 'ca'se you's hard up; you'll find you ain't gwyne to have no"
"3256"	"trouble. You take me up de country a piece, en sell me on a farm; dem"
"3257"	"people ain't gwyne to ask no questions if I's a bargain.\""
"3258"	"Tom forged a bill of sale and sold his mother to an Arkansas"
"3259"	"cotton-planter for a trifle over six hundred dollars. He did not want to"
"3260"	"commit this treachery, but luck threw the man in his way, and this saved"
"3261"	"him the necessity of going up country to hunt up a purchaser, with the"
"3262"	"added risk of having to answer a lot of questions, whereas this planter"
"3263"	"was so pleased with Roxy that he asked next to none at all. Besides, the"
"3264"	"planter insisted that Roxy wouldn't know where she was, at first, and"
"3265"	"that by the time she found out she would already have become contented."
"3266"	"And Tom argued with himself that it was an immense advantage for Roxy to"
"3267"	"have a master who was so pleased with her, as this planter manifestly"
"3268"	"was. In almost no time his flowing reasonings carried him to the point"
"3269"	"of even half believing he was doing Roxy a splendid surreptitious"
"3270"	"service in selling her \"down the river.\" And then he kept diligently"
"3271"	"saying to himself all the time: \"It's for only a year. In a year I buy"
"3272"	"her free again; she'll keep that in mind, and it'll reconcile her.\" Yes;"
"3273"	"the little deception could do no harm, and everything would come out"
"3274"	"right and pleasant in the end, any way. By agreement, the conversation"
"3275"	"in Roxy's presence was all about the man's \"upcountry\" farm, and how"
"3276"	"pleasant a place it was, and how happy the slaves were there; so poor"
"3277"	"Roxy was entirely deceived; and easily, for she was not dreaming that"
"3278"	"her own son could be guilty of treason to a mother who, in voluntarily"
"3279"	"going into slavery--slavery of any kind, mild or severe, or of any"
"3280"	"duration, brief or long--was making a sacrifice for him compared with"
"3281"	"which death would have been a poor and commonplace one. She lavished"
"3282"	"tears and loving caresses upon him privately, and then went away with"
"3283"	"her owner--went away broken-hearted, and yet proud of what she was"
"3284"	"doing, and glad it was in her power to do it."
"3285"	"Tom squared his accounts, and resolved to keep to the very letter of his"
"3286"	"reform, and never to put that will in jeopardy again. He had three"
"3287"	"hundred dollars left. According to his mother's plan, he was to put that"
"3288"	"safely away, and add her half of his pension to it monthly. In one year"
"3289"	"this fund would buy her free again."
"3290"	"For a whole week he was not able to sleep well, so much the villainy"
"3291"	"which he had played upon his trusting mother preyed upon his rag of a"
"3292"	"conscience; but after that he began to get comfortable again, and was"
"3293"	"presently able to sleep like any other miscreant."
"3294"	"The boat bore Roxy away from St. Louis at four in the afternoon, and she"
"3295"	"stood on the lower guard abaft the paddle-box and watched Tom through a"
"3296"	"blur of tears until he melted into the throng of people and disappeared;"
"3297"	"then she looked no more, but sat there on a coil of cable crying till"
"3298"	"far into the night. When she went to her foul steerage-bunk at last,"
"3299"	"between the clashing engines, it was not to sleep, but only to wait for"
"3300"	"the morning, and, waiting, grieve."
"3301"	"It had been imagined that she \"would not know,\" and would think she was"
"3302"	"traveling up stream. She! Why, she had been steamboating for years. At"
"3303"	"dawn she got up and went listlessly and sat down on the cable-coil"
"3304"	"again. She passed many a snag whose \"break\" could have told her a thing"
"3305"	"to break her heart, for it showed a current moving in the same direction"
"3306"	"that the boat was going; but her thoughts were elsewhere, and she did"
"3307"	"not notice. But at last the roar of a bigger and nearer break than usual"
"3308"	"brought her out of her torpor, and she looked up, and her practised eye"
"3309"	"fell upon that telltale rush of water. For one moment her petrified gaze"
"3310"	"fixed itself there. Then her head dropped upon her breast, and she"
"3311"	"said--"
"3312"	"\"Oh, de good Lord God have mercy on po' sinful me--I's sole down de"
"3313"	"river!\""
"3314"	"CHAPTER XVII."
"3315"	"The Judge Utters Dire Prophecy."
"3316"	"Even popularity can be overdone. In Rome, along at first, you are full"
"3317"	"of regrets that Michelangelo died; but by and by you only regret that"
"3318"	"you didn't see him do it.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"3319"	"July 4. Statistics show that we lose more fools on this day than in all"
"3320"	"the other days of the year put together. This proves, by the number left"
"3321"	"in stock, that one Fourth of July per year is now inadequate, the"
"3322"	"country has grown so.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's Calendar."
"3323"	"The summer weeks dragged by, and then the political campaign"
"3324"	"opened--opened in pretty warm fashion, and waxed hotter and hotter"
"3325"	"daily. The twins threw themselves into it with their whole heart, for"
"3326"	"their self-love was engaged. Their popularity, so general at first, had"
"3327"	"suffered afterward; mainly because they had been too popular, and so a"
"3328"	"natural reaction had followed. Besides, it had been diligently whispered"
"3329"	"around that it was curious--indeed, very curious--that that wonderful"
"3330"	"knife of theirs did not turn up--if it was so valuable, or if it had"
"3331"	"ever existed. And with the whisperings went chucklings and nudgings and"
"3332"	"winks, and such things have an effect. The twins considered that success"
"3333"	"in the election would reinstate them, and that defeat would work them"
"3334"	"irreparable damage. Therefore they worked hard, but not harder than"
"3335"	"Judge Driscoll and Tom worked against them in the closing days of the"
"3336"	"canvas. Tom's conduct had remained so letter-perfect during two whole"
"3337"	"months, now, that his uncle not only trusted him with money with which"
"3338"	"to persuade voters, but trusted him to go and get it himself out of the"
"3339"	"safe in the private sitting-room."
"3340"	"The closing speech of the campaign was made by Judge Driscoll, and he"
"3341"	"made it against both of the foreigners. It was disastrously effective."
"3342"	"He poured out rivers of ridicule upon them, and forced the big"
"3343"	"mass-meeting to laugh and applaud. He scoffed at them as adventurers,"
"3344"	"mountebanks, side-show riff-raff, dime museum freaks; he assailed their"
"3345"	"showy titles with measureless derision; he said they were back-alley"
"3346"	"barbers disguised as nobilities, peanut peddlers masquerading as"
"3347"	"gentlemen, organ-grinders bereft of their brother monkey. At last he"
"3348"	"stopped and stood still. He waited until the place had become absolutely"
"3349"	"silent and expectant, then he delivered his deadliest shot; delivered it"
"3350"	"with ice-cold seriousness and deliberation, with a significant emphasis"
"3351"	"upon the closing words: he said that he believed that the reward offered"
"3352"	"for the lost knife was humbug and buncombe, and that its owner would"
"3353"	"know where to find it whenever he should have occasion to assassinate"
"3354"	"somebody."
"3355"	"Then he stepped from the stand, leaving a startled and impressive hush"
"3356"	"behind him instead of the customary explosion of cheers and party cries."
"3357"	"The strange remark flew far and wide over the town and made an"
"3358"	"extraordinary sensation. Everybody was asking, \"What could he mean by"
"3359"	"that?\" And everybody went on asking that question, but in vain; for the"
"3360"	"Judge only said he knew what he was talking about, and stopped there;"
"3361"	"Tom said he hadn't any idea what his uncle meant, and Wilson, whenever"
"3362"	"he was asked what he thought it meant, parried the question by asking"
"3363"	"the questioner what he thought it meant."
"3364"	"Wilson was elected, the twins were defeated--crushed, in fact, and left"
"3365"	"forlorn and substantially friendless. Tom went back to St. Louis happy."
"3366"	"Dawson's Landing had a week of repose, now, and it needed it. But it was"
"3367"	"in an expectant state, for the air was full of rumors of a new duel."
"3368"	"Judge Driscoll's election labors had prostrated him, but it was said"
"3369"	"that as soon as he was well enough to entertain a challenge he would get"
"3370"	"one from Count Luigi."
"3371"	"The brothers withdrew entirely from society, and nursed their"
"3372"	"humiliation in privacy. They avoided the people, and went out for"
"3373"	"exercise only late at night, when the streets were deserted."
"3374"	"CHAPTER XVIII."
"3375"	"Roxana Commands."
"3376"	"Gratitude and treachery are merely the two extremities of the same"
"3377"	"procession. You have seen all of it that is worth staying for when the"
"3378"	"band and the gaudy officials have gone by.--Pudd'nhead Wilson's"
"3379"	"Calendar."
"3380"	"Thanksgiving Day. Let all give humble, hearty, and sincere thanks, now,"
"3381"	"but the turkeys. In the island of Fiji they do not use turkeys; they use"
"3382"	"plumbers. It does not become you and me to sneer at Fiji.--Pudd'nhead"
"3383"	"Wilson's Calendar."
"3384"	"The Friday after the election was a rainy one in St. Louis. It rained"
"3385"	"all day long, and rained hard, apparently trying its best to wash that"
"3386"	"soot-blackened town white, but of course not succeeding. Toward midnight"
"3387"	"Tom Driscoll arrived at his lodgings from the theatre in the heavy"
"3388"	"downpour, and closed his umbrella and let himself in; but when he would"
"3389"	"have shut the door, he found that there was another person"
"3390"	"entering--doubtless another lodger; this person closed the door and"
"3391"	"tramped up-stairs behind Tom. Tom found his door in the dark, and"
"3392"	"entered it and turned up the gas. When he faced about, lightly"
"3393"	"whistling, he saw the back of a man. The man was closing and locking his"
"3394"	"door for him. His whistle faded out and he felt uneasy. The man turned"
"3395"	"around, a wreck of shabby old clothes, sodden with rain and all a-drip,"
"3396"	"and showed a black face under an old slouch hat. Tom was frightened. He"
"3397"	"tried to order the man out, but the words refused to come, and the other"
"3398"	"man got the start. He said, in a low voice--"
"3399"	"\"Keep still--I's yo' mother!\""
"3400"	"Tom sunk in a heap on a chair, and gasped out--"
"3401"	"\"It was mean of me, and base--I know it; but I meant it for the best, I"
"3402"	"did indeed--I can swear it.\""
"3403"	"Roxana stood awhile looking mutely down on him while he writhed in shame"
"3404"	"and went on incoherently babbling self-accusations mixed with pitiful"
"3405"	"attempts at explanation and palliation of his crime; then she seated"
"3406"	"herself and took off her hat, and her unkept masses of long brown hair"
"3407"	"tumbled down about her shoulders."
"3408"	"\"It ain't no fault o' yo'n dat dat ain't gray,\" she said sadly, noticing"
"3409"	"the hair."
"3410"	"\"I know it, I know it! I'm a scoundrel. But I swear I meant it for the"
"3411"	"best. It was a mistake, of course, but I thought it was for the best, I"
"3412"	"truly did.\""
"3413"	"Roxana began to cry softly, and presently words began to find their way"
"3414"	"out between her sobs. They were uttered lamentingly, rather than"
"3415"	"angrily--"
"3416"	"\"Sell a pusson down de river--down the river!--for de bes'! I wouldn't"
"3417"	"treat a dog so! I is all broke down en wore out, now, en so I reckon it"
"3418"	"ain't in me to storm aroun' no mo', like I used to when I 'uz trompled"
"3419"	"on en 'bused. I don't know--but maybe it's so. Leastways, I's suffered"
"3420"	"so much dat mournin' seem to come mo' handy to me now den stormin'.\""
"3421"	"These words should have touched Tom Driscoll, but if they did, that"
"3422"	"effect was obliterated by a stronger one--one which removed the heavy"
"3423"	"weight of fear which lay upon him, and gave his crushed spirit a most"
"3424"	"grateful rebound, and filled all his small soul with a deep sense of"
"3425"	"relief. But he kept prudently still, and ventured no comment. There was"
"3426"	"a voiceless interval of some duration, now, in which no sounds were"
"3427"	"heard but the beating of the rain upon the panes, the sighing and"
"3428"	"complaining of the winds, and now and then a muffled sob from Roxana."
"3429"	"The sobs became more and more infrequent, and at last ceased. Then the"
"3430"	"refugee began to talk again:"
"3431"	"\"Shet down dat light a little. More. More yit. A pusson dat is hunted"
"3432"	"don't like de light. Dah--dat'll do. I kin see whah you is, en dat's"
"3433"	"enough. I's gwine to tell you de tale, en cut it jes as short as I kin,"
"3434"	"en den I'll tell you what you's got to do. Dat man dat bought me ain't a"
"3435"	"bad man; he's good enough, as planters goes; en if he could 'a' had his"
"3436"	"way I'd 'a' be'n a house servant in his fambly en be'n comfortable: but"
"3437"	"his wife she was a Yank, en not right down good lookin', en she riz up"
"3438"	"agin me straight off; so den dey sent me out to de quarter 'mongst de"
"3439"	"common fiel' han's. Dat woman warn't satisfied even wid dat, but she"
"3440"	"worked up de overseer ag'in' me, she 'uz dat jealous en hateful; so de"
"3441"	"overseer he had me out befo' day in de mawnin's en worked me de whole"
